class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>Molitor and Winfield, St. Paul natives and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a> graduates,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> came to the team late in their careers and were warmly received as "hometown heroes", but were elected to the Hall on the basis of their tenures with other teams. Both swatted their 3,000th hit with the Twins.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cronin, Goslin, Griffith, Harris, Johnson, Killebrew and Wynn are listed on the Washington Hall of Stars display at <a href="/wiki/Nationals_Park" title="Nationals Park">Nationals Park</a> (previously they were listed at <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Kennedy Stadium">Robert F. Kennedy Stadium</a>). So are <a href="/wiki/Ossie_Bluege" title="Ossie Bluege">Ossie Bluege</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Case" title="George Case">George Case</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Judge" title="Joe Judge">Joe Judge</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Selkirk" title="George Selkirk">George Selkirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Sievers" title="Roy Sievers">Roy Sievers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Travis" title="Cecil Travis">Cecil Travis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Vernon" title="Mickey Vernon">Mickey Vernon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Yost" title="Eddie Yost">Eddie Yost</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_C._Frick_Award_recipients">Ford C. Santana</a></td>\n<td>P</td>\n<td>2000\xe2\x80\x932007\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Twins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:758px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metrodome_curtain_of_fame.JPG" class="image" title="Banners and retired numbers displayed in the Metrodome"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Metrodome_curtain_of_fame.JPG/750px-Metrodome_curtain_of_fame.JPG" width="750" height="152" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/21/Metrodome_curtain_of_fame.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="1036" data-file-height="210" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metrodome_curtain_of_fame.JPG" title="File:Metrodome curtain of fame.JPG"> </a></div>Banners and retired numbers displayed in the Metrodome</div>\n</div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>\n<p>The Metrodome\'s upper deck in center and right fields was partly covered by a curtain containing banners of various titles won, and retired numbers. There was no acknowledgment of the Twins\' prior championships in Washington and several Senator Hall of Famers, such as Walter Johnson, played in the days prior to numbers being used on uniforms. However Killebrew played seven seasons as a Senator, including two full seasons as a regular prior to the move to Minnesota in 1961.\n</p><p>Prior to the addition of the banners, the Twins acknowledged their retired numbers on the Metrodome\'s outfield fence. Harmon Killebrew\'s #3 was the first to be displayed, as it was the only one the team had retired when they moved in. It was joined by Rod Carew\'s #29 in 1987, Tony Oliva\'s #6 in 1991, Kent Hrbek\'s #14 in 1995, and Kirby Puckett\'s #34 in 1997 before the Twins began hanging the banners to reduce capacity. The championships, meanwhile were marked on the "Baggie" in right field.\n</p>\n<table style="white-space:nowrap"><tbody><tr><td>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarmonKillebrewTwins.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/HarmonKillebrewTwins.png/100px-HarmonKillebrewTwins.png" width="100" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/HarmonKillebrewTwins.png/150px-HarmonKillebrewTwins.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/HarmonKillebrewTwins.png/200px-HarmonKillebrewTwins.png 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="560" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Harmon_Killebrew" title="Harmon Killebrew">Harmon<br />Killebrew</a><br />LF-1B-3B<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Honored <span style="white-space:nowrap">April 15, 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg/300px-Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg" width="300" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg/450px-Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg/600px-Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="420" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Field_04.12.2010_059_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Target Field retired number signs in 2010.</div></div></div><p> In the Metrodome, the numbers ran in that order from left to right. In Target Field, they run from right to left, presumably to allow space for additional numbers in the future. The retired numbers also serve as entry points at Target Field, The center field gate is Gate No. 3, honoring Killebrew, the left field gate is Gate No. 6, honoring Oliva, the home plate gate is Gate No. 14, for Hrbek, the right field gate serves as Gate No. 29, in tribute to Carew, and the plaza gate is known as Gate No. 34, honoring Puckett.\n</p><p>The numbers that have been retired hang within Target Field in front of the tower that serves as the Twins\' executive offices in left field foul territory. The championships banners have been replaced by small pennants that fly on masts at the back of the left field upper deck. Those pennants, along with the flags flying in the plaza behind right field, serve as a visual cue for the players, suggesting the wind direction and speed.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s number, 42, was retired by Major League Baseball on April 15, 1997 and formally honored by the Twins on May 23, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Robinson\'s number was positioned to the left of the Twins numbers in both venues.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" season">2017</a></td>\n<td>85</td>\n<td>77</td>\n<td>.525</td>\n<td>2nd&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 AL Central</td>\n<td>2,051,279</td>\n<td>25,324</td>\n<td>0\xe2\x80\x931</td>\n<td>.000</td>\n<td>Lost <a href="/wiki/2017_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2017 American League Wild Card Game">AL Wild Card Game</a> (<a href="/wiki/2017_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2017 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a>)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2018_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="2018 Minnesota Twins style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>4549</b></th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>4647</b></th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;">.495</th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x93</th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x93</th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x93</th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>25\xe2\x80\x9339</b></th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>.391</b></th>\n<th style="background-color:#D31E47;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>2 <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> Championships</b>\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Twins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Minnesota_Twins_broadcasters" title="List of Minnesota Twins broadcasters">List of Minnesota Twins broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>In 2007, the Twins took the rights to the broadcasts in-house and created the Twins Radio Network (TRN). With that new network in place the Twins secured a new Metro Affiliate <a href="/wiki/Flagship_(radio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagship (radio)">flagship</a> radio station in <a href="/wiki/KSTP_(AM)" title="KSTP (AM)">KSTP</a> (AM 1500). It replaced <a href="/wiki/WCCO_(AM)" title="WCCO (AM)">WCCO</a> (AM 830), which held broadcast rights for the Twins since the team moved to Minneapolis in 1961. For 2013, the Twins moved to FM radio on <a href="/wiki/KQGO" title="KQGO">KTWN-FM</a> <i>96.3 K-Twin</i>, which is owned by the Pohlad family. The original radio voices of the Twins in 1961 were <a href="/wiki/Ray_Scott_(sportscaster)" title="Ray Scott (sportscaster)">Ray Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halsey_Hall" title="Halsey Hall">Halsey Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wolff" title="Bob Wolff">Bob Wolff</a>. After the first season, <a href="/wiki/Herb_Carneal" title="Herb Carneal">Herb Carneal</a> replaced Wolff. Twins TV and radio broadcasts were originally sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Hamm%27s_Brewery" title="Hamm&#39;s Brewery">Hamm\'s Brewing Company</a>. In 2009, Treasure Island Resort &amp; Casino became the first ever naming rights partner for the Twins Radio Network, making the commercial name of TRN the Treasure Island Baseball Network.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, it was announced that WCCO would become the flagship station the Twins again starting in 2018, thus returning the team back to its original station after 11 years.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cory_Provus" title="Cory Provus">Cory Provus</a> is the current radio play by play announcer,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> taking over in 2012 for longtime Twins voice <a href="/wiki/John_Gordon_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Gordon (baseball)">John Gordon</a> who retired following the 2011 season.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Former Twins OF <a href="/wiki/Dan_Gladden" title="Dan Gladden">Dan Gladden</a> serves as color commentator.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>TRN broadcasts are originated from the studios at Minnesota News Network and Minnesota Farm Networks. Kris Atteberry hosts the pre-game show, the "Lineup Card" and the "Post-game Download" from those studios except when filling in for Provus or Gladden when they are on vacation.\n</p><p>On April 1, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Herb_Carneal" title="Herb Carneal">Herb Carneal</a>, the radio voice of the Twins for all but one year of their existence, died at his home in <a href="/wiki/Minnetonka,_Minnesota" title="Minnetonka, Minnesota">Minnetonka, Minnesota</a> after a long battle with a list of illnesses. Carneal is in the broadcasters wing of the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bert_Blyleven.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bert_Blyleven.jpg/220px-Bert_Blyleven.jpg" width="220" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bert_Blyleven.jpg/330px-Bert_Blyleven.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bert_Blyleven.jpg/440px-Bert_Blyleven.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1125" data-file-height="1105" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bert_Blyleven.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Bert_Blyleven" title="Bert Blyleven">Bert Blyleven</a> played 11 seasons for the Twins</div></div></div>\n<p>The television rights are held by <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_North" title="Fox Sports North">Fox Sports North</a><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Dick_Bremer" title="Dick Bremer">Dick Bremer</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcer and former Twin, 2011 <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a> inductee,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bert_Blyleven" title="Bert Blyleven">Bert Blyleven</a> as <a href="/wiki/Color_analyst" class="mw-redirect" title="Color analyst">color analyst</a>. They are sometimes joined by <a href="/wiki/Roy_Smalley_(AL_baseball_player)" class="mw-redirect" title="Roy Smalley (AL baseball player)">Roy Smalley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Morris" title="Jack Morris">Jack Morris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Casey_(baseball_announcer)" title="Bob Casey (baseball announcer)">Bob Casey</a> was the Twins first public-address announcer starting in 1961 and continuing until his death in 2005. He was well known for his unique delivery and his signature announcements of "No smoking in the Metrodome, either go outside or quit!" (or "go back to Boston", etc.), "Batting 3rd, the center-fielder, No. 34, Kirby Puckett!!!" and asking fans not to \'throw anything or anybody\' onto the field.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_activities">Community activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Twins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Community activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>Minnesota Twins Community Fund&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Play Ball! Minnesota<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_and_franchise_traditions">Team and franchise traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Twins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Team and franchise traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Fans wave a <i><a href="/wiki/Homer_Hanky" title="Homer Hanky">Homer Hanky</a></i> to rally the team during play-offs and other crucial games. The Homer Hanky was created by Terrie Robbins of the Star Tribune newspaper in the Twin Cities in 1987. It was her idea to originally give away 60,000 inaugural Homer Hankies. That year, over 2.3 million Homer Hankies were distributed.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The party atmosphere of the Twins clubhouse after a win is well-known,<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> the team\'s players unwinding with loud <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock music</a> (usually the choice of the winning <a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">pitcher</a>) and video games.<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The club has several <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a> rituals, such as requiring the most junior relief pitcher on the team to carry water and snacks to the bullpen in a brightly colored small child\'s backpack (<a href="/wiki/Barbie" title="Barbie">Barbie</a> in 2005, <a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants_(character)" title="SpongeBob SquarePants (character)">SpongeBob SquarePants</a> in 2006, <a href="/wiki/Hello_Kitty" title="Hello Kitty">Hello Kitty</a> in 2007, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tinkerbell" class="mw-redirect" title="Tinkerbell">Tinkerbell</a> in 2009, <a href="/wiki/Chewbacca" title="Chewbacca">Chewbacca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darth_Vader" title="Darth Vader">Darth Vader</a> in 2010),<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> and many of its players, both past and present, are notorious <a href="/wiki/Prank" class="mw-redirect" title="Prank">pranksters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwfoxsportsnorthcompagesvideoPIDFfjGlICsfpbRWWYXg_Suapv-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Bert_Blyleven" title="Bert Blyleven">Bert Blyleven</a> earned the nickname "The Frying Dutchman" for his ability to pull the "hotfoot"&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 which entails crawling under the bench in the dugout and lighting a teammate\'s shoelaces on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Twins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins_all-time_roster" title="Minnesota Twins all-time roster">Minnesota Twins all-time roster</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span
